< text>
Not a real ramen shop.
Place is as authentic of a ramen shop as Pizza Hut is an authentic Italian restaurant.
If you want ramen that is slightly better than Cup of Noodles for $15, then come here.
Menu is too big, chefs look like they are you typical $13/h "rent a chef" with no interest in this type of food.
Owner is probably clueless about cuisine, most likely some basic "investment only" type owner.
Place looks and feels passionless.
TIP - if you want GOOD ramen, find a place that ONLY serves ramen with a few side options. Not where ramen is half a page on a 20 page menu.</text>

The staff there was very friendly but unfortunately it was just two of them for the whole restaurant on a Sunday afternoon that didn't make sense to me at all it took them forever to even clean a table for example the table right next to me was dirty and had a bunch of dishes we were seated and about 20 minutes later they finally started cleaning up the table next to us that wasn't very pleasant looking at half-eaten bowls and having food left on the table so that's the reason for the one star drop. <Text>Very clean, stylish Japanese restaurant with a relatively simple menu featuring ramen, teriyaki, appetizers, and bento. The gyoza and shumai appetizers were delicate treats. Kid portions are available on select dishes, and the teriyaki salmon kid serving was an impressive six-ounce fillet with white rice and salad. Pork shoyu ramen was cooked and seasoned perfectly. < review>
Very small, the staff are really not friendly, or helpful at all. Made my first purchase 3 days ago at this location, of plates. It was a set that was packaged as 3 plates for a single price of $3.99, and I happened to find the 4th plate amidst a bunch of other plates as I was perusing for $2.99 for the single plate. I brought this to the cashier's attention and she stated, "you're getting a deal because I told them to price them at $2.99 each." This was clearly not true as all goodwills (including this one), puts obscene amounts of packing tapes on all dish sets and ALWAYS sells them as sets. They do not individually price items in sets at any Goodwill store I've been to (including this one). Which brings me to my next complaint. I also bought another "set" of 4 plates all packaging taped together, and when I got home one of the plates was terribly scratched (through the glaze and paint--the purple plate was scratched down to white ceramic). Knowing this was unsafe to eat off once the glaze and paint has been penetrated I attempted to return or exchange. I was told no at first, and I continued to complain that they shouldn't hide damaged items in a bundled package (online says you have 7 days with receipt and tab affixed, both of which was the case here). One of the "managers" then said, "ok find another item for the same price and I'll let you exchange as a one time courtesy credit."

Do you know what a pain it was to find an exactly same priced item? Unfortunately, I had already given them my donations outside as a I pulled up. I will now only give my business and donations to the Salvatian Army in Poway, where the staff is friendly, they offer delivery service of large furniture, have great flash sales, and will negotiate on prices, and allow returns with receipt. Much larger store, much better prices, friendly staff.< /review>

< Review>
New (tags on) and nearly new items with sparse size selections for proper prices makes this wisest choice for clothes, though you will be required to frequent the stores regularly to actually find specific articles you need.  With the epitome of inconsistent mechandise suppliers, one can only play the odds looking for more common things if time is limited.  Obviously quality tools and up to date electronics are not often found here, but many other necessities for life can be, and the savings there can leave more money for craigslist and offerup purchases of tools and newer electronic devices.
Retail prices have risen ridiculous amounts over the years, and I'm surprised these types of stores aren't more socially acceptable by now.</Review>

<Rating>5</Rating>< Text>
4/12/21 Note: this review is for the temporary covid vaccination site established at this location.
The vaccination site is very well organized with volunteers guiding candidates every step of the way. My appointment was at 10:45 and I was done with the shot at 10:53. You need to wait another 15 mins under observation for any reactions from the vaccine. There is a tent set up and seats are socially distanced for safety. Water bottles and candies are provided as well.
The site requires prior appointment and you need to have a consent form, a copy of a valid ID and your insurance.
This is a super smooth operation.<//Text>

<resp>None< /resp><date>1618599868294< /date>< review>
4/12/21 Note: this review is for the temporary covid vaccination site established at this location.
The vaccination site is very well organized with volunteers guiding candidates every step of the way. My appointment was at 10:45 and I was done with the shot at 10:53. You need to wait another 15 mins under observation for any reactions from the vaccine. There is a tent set up and seats are socially distanced for safety. Water bottles and candies are provided as well.
The site requires prior appointment and you need to have a consent form, a copy of a valid ID and your insurance.
This is a super smooth operation.</review>
